/></a></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><b>EasyJet plc</b>, styled as <b>easyJet</b>, is a British multinational <a href="/wiki/Low-cost_carrier" title="Low-cost carrier">low-cost airline</a> group headquartered at <a href="/wiki/London_Luton_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="London Luton Airport">London Luton Airport</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> It operates domestic and international scheduled services on over 1,000 routes in more than 30 countries via its affiliate airlines <a href="/wiki/EasyJet_UK" title="EasyJet UK">EasyJet UK</a>, <a href="/wiki/EasyJet_Switzerland" title="EasyJet Switzerland">EasyJet Switzerland</a>, and <a href="/wiki/EasyJet_Europe" title="EasyJet Europe">EasyJet Europe</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ADB_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ADB-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> EasyJet plc is listed on the <a href="/wiki/London_Stock_Exchange" title="London Stock Exchange">London Stock Exchange</a> and is a constituent of the <a href="/wiki/FTSE_250_Index" title="FTSE 250 Index">FTSE 250 Index</a>. <a href="/wiki/EasyGroup" title="EasyGroup">EasyGroup</a> Holdings Ltd (the investment vehicle of the airline\'s founder, Greek-Cypriot businessman <a href="/wiki/Stelios_Haji-Ioannou" title="Stelios Haji-Ioannou">Stelios Haji-Ioannou</a>, and his family) is the largest shareholder with a 29.998% stake (as of June 2020).<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> It employs circa 14,000 people, based throughout Europe but mainly in the UK.<sup id="cite_ref-what_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-what-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>EasyJet has seen expansion since its establishment in 1995, having grown through a combination of <a href="/wiki/Mergers_and_acquisitions" title="Mergers and acquisitions">acquisitions</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-GO1_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GO1-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-GB1_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GB1-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> and base openings fuelled by consumer demand for low-cost air travel. The group, along with associate companies <a href="/wiki/EasyJet_UK" title="EasyJet UK">EasyJet UK</a>, <a href="/wiki/EasyJet_Europe" title="EasyJet Europe">EasyJet Europe</a> and <a href="/wiki/EasyJet_Switzerland" title="EasyJet Switzerland">EasyJet Switzerland</a>, operate more than 300 aircraft. It has 29 bases across Europe, the largest being <a href="/wiki/Gatwick_Airport" title="Gatwick Airport">Gatwick</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-bases_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bases-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> In 2014, the airline carried more than 65&#160;million passengers,<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> making it the second-largest budget airline in Europe by number of passengers carried, behind <a href="/wiki/Ryanair" title="Ryanair">Ryanair</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>EasyJet was featured in the television series <i><a href="/wiki/Airline_(UK_TV_series)" class="mw-redirect" title="Airline (UK TV series)">Airline</a></i> broadcast on <a href="/wiki/ITV_(TV_network)" title="ITV (TV network)">ITV</a> which followed the airline\'s operations at London Luton and later at other bases. Its pilot training scheme was the subject of another ITV television series, <i><a href="/wiki/EasyJet:_Inside_the_Cockpit" title="EasyJet: Inside the Cockpit">easyJet: Inside the Cockpit</a></i>, which premiered in August 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 30 March 2020, EasyJet grounded its entire fleet of planes due to the <a href="/wiki/COVID-19_pandemic" title="COVID-19 pandemic">COVID-19 pandemic</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> They later closed three of their bases.<sup id="cite_ref-Aug20_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Aug20-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc" role="navigation" class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=EasyJet&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Origins_and_formation">Origins and formation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=EasyJet&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Origins and formation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>EasyJet has its roots in the business activity of <a href="/wiki/Greeks" title="Greeks">Greek</a>-<a href="/wiki/Greek_Cypriots" title="Greek Cypriots">Cypriot</a> <a href="/wiki/Stelios_Haji-Ioannou" title="Stelios Haji-Ioannou">Stelios Haji-Ioannou</a>, who reportedly gained an interest in the aviation business after being approached as a potential <a href="/wiki/Investor" title="Investor">investor</a> in <a href="/wiki/Virgin_Atlantic" title="Virgin Atlantic">Virgin Atlantic</a>\'s Greek franchisee. Recognising a vacant niche in the market, Stelios decided to examine the prospects for launching his own airline, having secured a commitment of a \xc2\xa35 million ($7.7 million) loan from his father.<sup id="cite_ref-managementtoday_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-managementtoday-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> While studying various business models in the industry, Stelios took significant interest in the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">American</a> operator <a href="/wiki/Southwest_Airlines" title="Southwest Airlines">Southwest Airlines</a>, which had successfully adopted the practice of price elasticity to be competitive with traditionally cheaper buses and attract customers that wouldn\'t normally have considered air travel. This principle became a cornerstone of EasyJet\'s operations.<sup id="cite_ref-managementtoday_15-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-managementtoday-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1995, EasyJet was established by Stelios, being the first company in what would later become the <a href="/wiki/EasyGroup" title="EasyGroup">easyGroup</a> conglomerate. Upon launch, it employed just 70 people; the company being based at <a href="/wiki/London_Luton_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="London Luton Airport">London Luton Airport</a>, which was traditionally used only by <a href="/wiki/Charter" title="Charter">charter</a> flights.<sup id="cite_ref-managementtoday_15-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-managementtoday-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-20_telegraph_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20_telegraph-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> To encourage the company, Luton Airport chose to give EasyJet free use of a 15,000 square feet building for its headquarters, which it named <i>easyLand</i>; its management style typified minimal <a href="/wiki/Overhead_(business)" title="Overhead (business)">overhead</a>, such as an early implementation of the <a href="/wiki/Paperless_office" title="Paperless office">paperless office</a> concept.<sup id="cite_ref-managementtoday_15-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-managementtoday-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> EasyJet initially operated a pair of <a href="/wiki/Wet_lease" class="mw-redirect" title="Wet lease">wet leased</a> <a href="/wiki/Boeing_737" title="Boeing 737">Boeing 737-200</a> aircraft, capable of seating 130 passengers. These were flown on two routes: Luton to <a href="/wiki/Glasgow_International_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Glasgow International Airport">Glasgow</a> and <a href="/wiki/Edinburgh_Airport" title="Edinburgh Airport">Edinburgh</a>. Early on, EasyJet operated as a \'paper airline\', the aircraft themselves being flown and maintained under a lease.<sup id="cite_ref-managementtoday_15-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-managementtoday-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Early promotional activity focused on the airline\'s relatively low pricing in comparison to incumbent operators.<sup id="cite_ref-20_telegraph_17-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20_telegraph-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> Within its first year, easyJet reportedly carried approximately 40,000 passengers.<sup id="cite_ref-20_telegraph_17-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20_telegraph-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In April 1996, the first wholly owned aircraft was delivered to EasyJet, enabling the company\'s first international route, to <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam" title="Amsterdam">Amsterdam</a>, which was operated in direct competition with rival airlines <a href="/wiki/British_Airways" title="British Airways">British Airways</a> (BA) and <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">Dutch</a> <a href="/wiki/Flag_carrier" title="Flag carrier">flag carrier</a> <a href="/wiki/KLM" title="KLM">KLM</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-managementtoday_15-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-managementtoday-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-20_telegraph_17-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20_telegraph-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> Competitors responded to the emerging EasyJet in different ways; while BA was largely indifferent, KLM allegedly chose to respond with a <a href="/wiki/Predatory_pricing" title="Predatory pricing">predatory pricing</a> <a href="/wiki/Pricing_strategies" title="Pricing strategies">strategy</a> that led to an investigation by the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> over unfair competitive practices.<sup id="cite_ref-managementtoday_15-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-managementtoday-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> Despite commercial pressure from the emergent no-frills sector, traditional airlines have been unable to directly adopt similar practices to EasyJet due to vigorous protection of existing employee privileges by <a href="/wiki/Trade_union" title="Trade union">unions</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Until October 1997, all of EasyJet\'s aircraft were operated by <a href="/wiki/GB_Airways" title="GB Airways">GB Airways</a>, and subsequently by <a href="/wiki/Monarch_Airlines" title="Monarch Airlines">Monarch Airlines</a> and <a href="/wiki/Air_Foyle" class="mw-redirect" title="Air Foyle">Air Foyle</a>, as EasyJet had not yet received its <a href="/wiki/Air_Operator%27s_Certificate" class="mw-redirect" title="Air Operator&#39;s Certificate">Air Operator\'s Certificate</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-KE_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KE-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Floatation">Floatation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=EasyJet&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Floatation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>On 5 November 2000, EasyJet was floated on the <a href="/wiki/London_Stock_Exchange" title="London Stock Exchange">London Stock Exchange</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-KE_19-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KE-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> In October 2004, the <a href="/wiki/FL_Group" class="mw-redirect" title="FL Group">FL Group</a>, owner of the airlines <a href="/wiki/Icelandair" title="Icelandair">Icelandair</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sterling_Airlines" title="Sterling Airlines">Sterling</a>, purchased an 8.4% stake in the airline.<sup id="cite_ref-fl_group_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fl_group-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> Over the course of 2005, FL increased its share in the company periodically to 16.9%,<sup id="cite_ref-fl_group_20-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fl_group-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> fuelling speculation that it would mount a takeover bid for the UK carrier.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> However, in April 2006, the threat of takeover receded as FL sold its stake for \xe2\x82\xac325&#160;million, securing a profit of \xe2\x82\xac140m on its investment.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In March 2013, EasyJet was promoted to the <a href="/wiki/FTSE_100" class="mw-redirect" title="FTSE 100">FTSE 100</a>; during the same month, the company launched its 100th route from Gatwick Airport, offering flights directly from London to <a href="/wiki/Moscow" title="Moscow">Moscow</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> By 2015, the company was flying routes to more than 130 destinations in 31 countries, operated 26 bases centred around Europe, and had a total of 10,000 employees.<sup id="cite_ref-20_telegraph_17-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20_telegraph-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Expansion_and_acquisitions">Expansion and acquisitions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=EasyJet&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Expansion and acquisitions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Go_Fly_Boeing_737-300_G-IGOB_departing_Bristol_Airport_in_2004.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Go_Fly_Boeing_737-300_G-IGOB_departing_Bristol_Airport_in_2004.jpg/220px-Go_Fly_Boeing_737-300_G-IGOB_departing_Bristol_Airport_in_2004.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="157" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Go_Fly_Boeing_737-300_G-IGOB_departing_Bristol_Airport_in_2004.jpg/330px-Go_Fly_Boeing_737-300_G-IGOB_departing_Bristol_Airport_in_2004.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Go_Fly_Boeing_737-300_G-IGOB_departing_Bristol_Airport_in_2004.jpg/440px-Go_Fly_Boeing_737-300_G-IGOB_departing_Bristol_Airport_in_2004.jpg 2x" data-file-width="750" data-file-height="536" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Go_Fly_Boeing_737-300_G-IGOB_departing_Bristol_Airport_in_2004.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A <a href="/wiki/Go_(airline)" title="Go (airline)">Go Fly</a> <a href="/wiki/Boeing_737_Classic" title="Boeing 737 Classic">Boeing 737-300</a> in 2004</div></div></div>\n<p>In March 1998, EasyJet purchased a 40% stake in Swiss charter airline <a href="/wiki/TEA_Basle" class="mw-redirect" title="TEA Basle">TEA Basle</a> for three million <a href="/wiki/Swiss_franc" title="Swiss franc">Swiss francs</a>. The airline was renamed <a href="/wiki/EasyJet_Switzerland" title="EasyJet Switzerland">EasyJet Switzerland</a> and commenced <a href="/wiki/Franchising" title="Franchising">franchise</a> services on 1 April 1999, having relocated its headquarters to <a href="/wiki/Geneva_International_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Geneva International Airport">Geneva International Airport</a>. Geneva was EasyJet\'s first new base outside the United Kingdom.<sup id="cite_ref-KE_19-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KE-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> In 2002, rival airline <a href="/wiki/Go_(airline)" title="Go (airline)">Go Fly</a> was purchased for \xc2\xa3374&#160;million; the airline inherited three new bases from Go, at <a href="/wiki/Bristol_Airport" title="Bristol Airport">Bristol Airport</a>, <a href="/wiki/East_Midlands_Airport" title="East Midlands Airport">East Midlands Airport</a> and <a href="/wiki/London_Stansted_Airport" title="London Stansted Airport">London Stansted Airport</a>; the acquisition of Go almost doubled the number of <a href="/wiki/Boeing_737_Classic" title="Boeing 737 Classic">Boeing 737-300</a> aircraft in the EasyJet fleet.<sup id="cite_ref-GO1_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GO1-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2002, the airline opened its base at <a href="/wiki/Gatwick_Airport" title="Gatwick Airport">Gatwick Airport</a>. Between 2003 and 2007, it opened additional bases in Germany, France, Italy, and Spain, establishing a presence in continental Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-KE_19-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KE-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> By 2007, EasyJet was claiming to be operating more flights per day than any other European airline.<sup id="cite_ref-Bamber,_G.J.,_Gittell,_J.H.,_Kochan,_T.A._&amp;_von_Nordenflytch,_A._2009_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bamber,_G.J.,_Gittell,_J.H.,_Kochan,_T.A._&amp;_von_Nordenflytch,_A._2009-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 25 October 2007, EasyJet purchased the entire share capital of <a href="/wiki/GB_Airways" title="GB Airways">GB Airways</a> from the <a href="/wiki/Bland_Group" title="Bland Group">Bland Group</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> This acquisition was valued at \xc2\xa3103.5&#160;million, and was used by the airline to expand its operations at Gatwick,<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> and to establish a base at <a href="/wiki/Manchester_Airport" title="Manchester Airport">Manchester Airport</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-GB1_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GB1-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-GB2_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GB2-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-GB3_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GB3-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-GB4_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GB4-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In June 2011, the airline opened its eleventh British base &#8211; at <a href="/wiki/London_Southend_Airport" title="London Southend Airport">London Southend Airport</a>, offering flights to <a href="/wiki/Alicante" title="Alicante">Alicante</a>, Amsterdam, <a href="/wiki/Barcelona" title="Barcelona">Barcelona</a>, <a href="/wiki/Belfast" title="Belfast">Belfast</a>, <a href="/wiki/Faro,_Portugal" title="Faro, Portugal">Faro</a>, <a href="/wiki/M%C3%A1laga" title="M\xc3\xa1laga">M\xc3\xa1laga</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jersey" title="Jersey">Jersey</a>, <a href="/wiki/Palma_de_Mallorca" title="Palma de Mallorca">Palma de Mallorca</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ibiza" title="Ibiza">Ibiza</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In July 2017, EasyJet announced it would open a new European headquarters in <a href="/wiki/Austria" title="Austria">Austria</a> to enable it to operate after <a href="/wiki/Brexit" title="Brexit">Brexit</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 28 October 2017, EasyJet announced it will lease 25 former <a href="/wiki/Air_Berlin" title="Air Berlin">Air Berlin</a> A320 aircraft to operate across <a href="/wiki/EasyJet_Europe" title="EasyJet Europe">EasyJet Europe</a>\'s network, under its European AOC. Several of these aircraft were based at <a href="/wiki/Berlin_Tegel_Airport" title="Berlin Tegel Airport">Berlin-Tegel Airport</a>, before its closure. These aircraft have subsequently been transferred to <a href="/wiki/Berlin_Brandenburg_Airport" title="Berlin Brandenburg Airport">Berlin-Brandenburg Airport</a>. Previously EasyJet had only operated from <a href="/wiki/Berlin_Sch%C3%B6nefeld_Airport" title="Berlin Sch\xc3\xb6nefeld Airport">Berlin-Sch\xc3\xb6nefeld Airport</a> and <a href="/wiki/Berlin_Tegel_Airport" title="Berlin Tegel Airport">Berlin-Tegel Airport</a>, where EasyJet had taken over some of Air Berlin\'s old services.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 30 March 2020, EasyJet suspended all flights, grounded its entire fleet, and furloughed its crews due to travel restrictions imposed. <sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> This came after the company had flown 650 \'rescue flights\', taking 45,000 people back home.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> In April 2020 EasyJet secured a \xc2\xa3600 million loan from the <a href="/wiki/UK_Government" class="mw-redirect" title="UK Government">UK Government</a> with no environmental conditions attached.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> In June 2020, EasyJet announced their intention to resume flights, flying half of their routes in July 2020 and up to 75 per cent in August 2020, though with reduced frequency.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In April 2020, EasyJet became involved in a dispute with its owner and largest shareholder, Stelios Haji-Ioannou. Haji-Ioannou criticised the airline\'s decision not to seek to cancel the outstanding Airbus order, claiming it would create an additional \xc2\xa34.5bn of capital which the airline could not afford to spend. He threatened to call a general meeting to remove a director every three weeks unless subsequent action was taken. A general meeting was held on 22 May, where shareholders ultimately voted over 99% in favour of the EasyJet board and retaining the Airbus contract.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 19 May 2020, the company revealed that it had been the subject of a <a href="/wiki/Cyber-attack" class="mw-redirect" title="Cyber-attack">cyber-attack</a> resulting in the release of the personal information of 9 million customers.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 17 August 2020, EasyJet confirmed in a statement they would be closing three bases in the UK. <a href="/wiki/London_Stansted_Airport" title="London Stansted Airport">Stansted</a>, <a href="/wiki/London_Southend_Airport" title="London Southend Airport">Southend</a>, as well as <a href="/wiki/Newcastle_International_Airport" title="Newcastle International Airport">Newcastle</a> from the end of August due to low levels of air travel demand impacted by the <a href="/wiki/COVID-19_pandemic" title="COVID-19 pandemic">COVID-19 pandemic</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Aug20_14-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Aug20-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Corporate_affairs">Corporate affairs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=EasyJet&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Corporate affairs">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Business_strategy">Business strategy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=EasyJet&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Business strategy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>EasyJet, like <a href="/wiki/Ryanair" title="Ryanair">Ryanair</a>, uses a business model pioneered by <a href="/wiki/Southwest_Airlines" title="Southwest Airlines">Southwest Airlines</a>. Both airlines have adapted this model for the European market through further cost-cutting measures, such as not selling connecting flights or providing complimentary snacks on board. The key points of this business model are high aircraft utilisation, quick turnaround times, charging for extras (such as priority boarding, hold baggage, and food) and keeping operating costs low.<sup id="cite_ref-YEALD_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-YEALD-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> One main difference EasyJet and Ryanair have from Southwest is they both fly a young fleet of aircraft. Southwest has an average fleet age of 11.9 years<sup id="cite_ref-swaage_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-swaage-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> whereas Ryanair\'s and EasyJet\'s average fleet ages are just a little over six years each.<sup id="cite_ref-Airline_Fleet_Age_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Airline_Fleet_Age-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Initially, EasyJet\'s employment strategy was to maintain control with minimal union involvement. During the 2000s, the airline adopted a different approach, deciding to make accommodations for unions.<sup id="cite_ref-Bamber,_G.J.,_Gittell,_J.H.,_Kochan,_T.A._&amp;_von_Nordenflytch,_A._2009_25-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bamber,_G.J.,_Gittell,_J.H.,_Kochan,_T.A._&amp;_von_Nordenflytch,_A._2009-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Originally, much like Southwest, EasyJet did not allocate seats \xe2\x80\x93 passengers took any available seats, with the option to pay for "Speedy Boarding", which allowed them to be first onto the aircraft. Since 2012, all passengers are allocated numbered seats before boarding commences, as it was found that this does not slow down boarding times and could earn more revenue than Speedy Boarding. Passengers can pay an additional fee for certain seats such as the front few rows and overwing seats (which have extra legroom).<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Financial_performance">Financial performance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=EasyJet&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Financial performance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Since the start of the <a href="/wiki/COVID-19_pandemic" title="COVID-19 pandemic">COVID-19 pandemic</a> until August 2020, EasyJet raised over \xc2\xa32.4 billion in new finance. Out of the sum, \xc2\xa3600 million came from the Covid Corporate Financing Facility provided by the UK government and over \xc2\xa3400m were raised from placement of shares.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> In November 2020, EasyJet announced that, due to the pandemic and the lockdowns in many countries, it would scale back its reduced flying schedule to no more than 20 percent of capacity.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> It also announced its first annual loss during the 25 year-history of the company.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable" style="clear: both">\n<caption><b>EasyJet financial 2000\n</td>\n<td>5,600,000\n</td>\n<td>\n</td>\n<td>263.7\n</td>\n<td>22.1\n</td>\n<td>22.1\n</td>\n<td>11.9\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Head_office">Head office</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=EasyJet&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Head office">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:EasyJetHQ.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/EasyJetHQ.jpg/220px-EasyJetHQ.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/EasyJetHQ.jpg/330px-EasyJetHQ.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/EasyJetHQ.jpg/440px-EasyJetHQ.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="480" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:EasyJetHQ.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Hangar 89 at <a href="/wiki/London_Luton_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="London Luton Airport">London Luton Airport</a>, EasyJet\'s head office.</div></div></div>\n<p>EasyJet\'s head office is Hangar 89 (H89), a building located on the grounds of <a href="/wiki/London_Luton_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="London Luton Airport">London Luton Airport</a> in <a href="/wiki/Luton" title="Luton">Luton</a>, Bedfordshire; the hangar is located 150 metres (490&#160;ft) from EasyLand, the previous headquarters of the airline. Hangar 89, built in 1974, has 30,000 square feet (2,800&#160;m<sup>2</sup>) of office space and can house three aircraft the size of an Airbus A319 at one time. When EasyJet received H89, it had a 1970s-style office setup. The airline modernised the building and painted it orange.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Marketing">Marketing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=EasyJet&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Marketing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>EasyJet\'s early marketing slogan was "making flying as affordable as a pair of jeans". It urged travellers to cut out the travel agent. Its original advertising consisted of little more than the airline\'s telephone booking number painted in bright orange on the side of its aircraft.<sup id="cite_ref-KE_19-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KE-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> The specific color that EasyJet uses closely resembles that of the telecommunications corporation <a href="/wiki/Orange_S.A." title="Orange S.A.">Orange</a> and was a subject of dispute between the two companies in 2004 when easyGroup launched a mobile phone subsidiary, <a href="/wiki/EasyGroup#EasyMobile" title="EasyGroup">easyMobile</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <i><a href="/wiki/Airline_(UK_TV_series)" class="mw-redirect" title="Airline (UK TV series)">Airline</a></i> TV series created by <a href="/wiki/LWT" class="mw-redirect" title="LWT">LWT</a> and filmed between 1999 and 2007 made EasyJet a household name in the United Kingdom. The series, while not always portraying the airline in a positive light, did much to promote it during this time.<sup id="cite_ref-ARL_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ARL-51">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> The airline has used a number of <a href="/wiki/Slogan" title="Slogan">slogans</a> since its establishment, including "The Web\'s Favourite Airline", "Come on, let\'s fly" and "To Fly, To Save" (a parody of <a href="/wiki/British_Airways" title="British Airways">British Airways\'</a> slogan "To Fly, To Serve"). This was then followed by "[....] by easyJet", with "Europe by easyJet" and "business by easyJet" being the most widely used. It currently uses the slogan "This is Generation easyJet".<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Environment">Environment</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=EasyJet&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Environment">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In June 2007, EasyJet announced plans for the construction of its own airliner, dubbed <i>EcoJet</i>. It was claimed to possess improved <a href="/wiki/Fuel_efficiency" title="Fuel efficiency">fuel efficiency</a> over contemporary airliners. To achieve this, the EcoJet was described as using <a href="/wiki/Propfan" title="Propfan">propfan</a> engines, as well as being constructed with extensive use of <a href="/wiki/Carbon_fibre" class="mw-redirect" title="Carbon fibre">carbon fibre</a> <a href="/wiki/Composite_material" title="Composite material">composite material</a>. At the time of the announcement, it was stated that the <a href="/wiki/Maiden_flight" title="Maiden flight">first flight</a> was scheduled to occur sometime during 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> Speaking at the time, EasyJet chief executive Andy Harrison commented that: "We have not developed a new concept. We have taken ideas from Boeing, Airbus and the engine manufacturers and put them together." Harrison claimed that the EcoJet, combined with other improvements in the industry, would enable a 50% reduction in <a href="/wiki/Greenhouse_gas_emissions" title="Greenhouse gas emissions">greenhouse gas emissions</a> within eight years.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> However, there has been few announcements on the project since then.<sup id="cite_ref-raeshort_2017_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-raeshort_2017-56">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In February 2011, the airline painted eight of its aircraft with a lightweight, thin "revolutionary nano technology coating" <a href="/wiki/Polymer" title="Polymer">polymer</a>. It works by reducing the build-up of debris and reduces <a href="/wiki/Drag_(physics)" title="Drag (physics)">drag</a> across the surface of the aircraft, thus reducing the fuel bill. It was estimated the airline could save 1\xe2\x80\x932% annually, equating to a \xc2\xa314&#160;million reduction in fuel costs. The coating has already been used on US military aircraft and if successful EasyJet would apply the paint to its whole fleet.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> In late 2015, EasyJet started making use of <a href="/wiki/Artificial_intelligence" title="Artificial intelligence">artificial intelligence</a> (AI) and <a href="/wiki/Big_data" title="Big data">big data</a> for the purpose of improving efficiency, cutting costs, and enhancing the customer experience.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 27 September 2017, EasyJet announced its partnership with an <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">American</a> start-up company <a href="/wiki/Wright_Electric" title="Wright Electric">Wright Electric</a> with the purpose of developing and introducing a short-haul 120-seat all-electric airline.<sup id="cite_ref-raeshort_2017_56-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-raeshort_2017-56">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> The propulsion system is said to comprise a series of eight electrically driven <a href="/wiki/Ducted_fan" title="Ducted fan">ducted fans</a> that are buried in the wings, which are powered by numerous <a href="/wiki/Electric_battery" title="Electric battery">battery</a> packs distributed underneath the cabin floor; it is claimed to possess a range of roughly 335 miles, suitable for about one-fifth of EasyJet\'s current city routes, and facilitate zero-emission flights, as well as being 50% quieter and 10% less expensive to operate than conventional jet airliners. At the time, EasyJet stated that it intended to introduce the electric aircraft into revenue service within 10 years.<sup id="cite_ref-raeshort_2017_56-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-raeshort_2017-56">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> In October 2018, EasyJet stated that progress was being made on its electric ambitions, and that the partnerships planned to test a nine-seater electric plane as early as 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Since November 2019, easyJet has offset the carbon emissions from all of its flights using carbon offsetting projects that meet either the Gold Standard or Verified Carbon Standard (VCS) accreditation. As a result, it is the first major airline in the world to operate net-carbon zero flights across its entire network.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> The airline describes this as an "interim" measure whilst the next generation of aircraft propulsion is developed. Consequently, easyJet announced a partnership with Airbus on a joint research project into zero-emission hydrogen aircraft.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Criticism">Criticism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=EasyJet&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Criticism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>EasyJet has been criticised in Germany for not observing <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> law on compensation (and assistance to passengers) in cases of denied boarding, delays or cancellations (<a href="/wiki/Regulation_261/2004" class="mw-redirect" title="Regulation 261/2004">Regulation 261/2004</a>). When flights are cancelled, passengers are supposed to be reimbursed within one week. In 2006, the airline did not always refund tickets in a timely fashion. Passengers occasionally had to wait longer for reimbursement of their expenses.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>EasyJet has campaigned for the UK to replace <a href="/wiki/Air_passenger_duty" class="mw-redirect" title="Air passenger duty">air passenger duty</a> (APD) with a new tax that would vary depending on distance travelled and aircraft type.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In July 2008, the <a href="/wiki/Advertising_Standards_Authority_(United_Kingdom)" title="Advertising Standards Authority (United Kingdom)">United Kingdom Advertising Standards Authority</a> (ASA) criticised a press campaign by the airline, over a misleading environmental claim that its aircraft released 22% fewer emissions than rival airlines. The figures used were not based on emissions produced by an EasyJet aircraft or emissions produced by the airline overall as the advertisement implied, and ASA declared that the airline had broken advertising rules. The judgement that followed reprimanded the airline in April 2007 after it made comments that its aircraft created 30% less pollution per passenger than some of its rivals.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In July 2011, the airline tried to refuse carriage of a boy with <a href="/wiki/Muscular_dystrophy" title="Muscular dystrophy">muscular dystrophy</a> because he had an electric wheelchair.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> In separate incidents in 2012, <a href="/wiki/Paralympian" class="mw-redirect" title="Paralympian">paralympians</a> received similar treatment,<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> and a French court found the airline guilty of three counts of disability discrimination.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> In January 2017, the company was fined \xe2\x82\xac60,000 by another French court because it had refused to allow a disabled passenger to board in 2010; the company cited security concerns and internal regulations, but said it would not appeal against the ruling.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In September 2013, a passenger who sent a tweet complaining about the airline after his flight was delayed said he was initially told he would not be allowed to board the aircraft because of the posting.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 27 August 2020, the airline was sued by a woman over discriminatory concerns. The woman had been asked to switch seats twice in a row, in order to accommodate two ultra-Orthodox Jewish men.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="European_AOC">European AOC</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=EasyJet&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: European AOC">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:EasyJet_Europe_Airbus_A319_(OE-LQQ)_arrives_Bristol_Airport_14May2019.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/EasyJet_Europe_Airbus_A319_%28OE-LQQ%29_arrives_Bristol_Airport_14May2019.JPG/220px-EasyJet_Europe_Airbus_A319_%28OE-LQQ%29_arrives_Bristol_Airport_14May2019.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="139" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/EasyJet_Europe_Airbus_A319_%28OE-LQQ%29_arrives_Bristol_Airport_14May2019.JPG/330px-EasyJet_Europe_Airbus_A319_%28OE-LQQ%29_arrives_Bristol_Airport_14May2019.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/EasyJet_Europe_Airbus_A319_%28OE-LQQ%29_arrives_Bristol_Airport_14May2019.JPG/440px-EasyJet_Europe_Airbus_A319_%28OE-LQQ%29_arrives_Bristol_Airport_14May2019.JPG 2x" data-file-width="4311" data-file-height="2732" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:EasyJet_Europe_Airbus_A319_(OE-LQQ)_arrives_Bristol_Airport_14May2019.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>An <a href="/wiki/EasyJet_Europe" title="EasyJet Europe">EasyJet Europe</a> <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A319" title="Airbus A319">Airbus A319</a> arrives at <a href="/wiki/Bristol_International_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Bristol International Airport">Bristol Airport</a> in May 2019. This aircraft is registered in Austria as OE-LQQ.</div></div></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/EasyJet_Europe" title="EasyJet Europe">EasyJet Europe</a></div>\n<p>Following the UK\'s referendum vote to leave the European Union, EasyJet announced plan to establish an Air Operator Certificate (AOC) in another EU member state. This will secure the flying rights of the 30% of EasyJet\'s network that remains wholly within and between EU states, excluding the UK. EasyJet expects a one-off cost of around \xc2\xa310 million over two years with up to \xc2\xa35 million incurred in the 2017 financial year. The primary driver of the cost is the re-registering of aircraft in an EU AOC jurisdiction.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> In July 2017, EasyJet announced that it has applied for, and was subsequently granted by the <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Transport_(Austria)" class="mw-redirect" title="Ministry of Transport (Austria)">Ministry of Transport</a>, an Austrian Air Operator Certificate (AOC) and operating permit, thereby establishing <a href="/wiki/EasyJet_Europe" title="EasyJet Europe">EasyJet Europe</a>. The new airline is headquartered in Vienna, and will allow EasyJet to continue operating flights across and within European countries after the UK leaves the EU. The first aircraft, an Airbus A320, was re-registered as OE-IVA.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>EasyJet announced that the transition would result in no job losses in the UK, as the staff to be employed by EasyJet Europe are already based in the EU27. <a href="/wiki/EasyJet_UK" title="EasyJet UK">EasyJet UK</a> staff would continue to be based in Luton. The group will thus comprise three airlines, EasyJet UK, EasyJet Europe, and EasyJet Switzerland, all of which are owned by EasyJet plc, which is itself EU owned and controlled, listed on the London Stock Exchange, and based in the UK.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> In May 2018, EasyJet confirmed that it was very close to achieving the required majority EU27 share ownership, and that the UK government will nevertheless continue to consider it as a UK airline.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Destinations">Destinations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=EasyJet&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Destinations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_EasyJet_destinations" title="List of EasyJet destinations">List of EasyJet destinations</a></div>\n<table class="wikitable International Airport">Belfast</a></td>\n<td>BFS</td>\n<td>37\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>EasyJet serves 136 destinations (as of February 2019).<sup id="cite_ref-EasyJet_Route_Map_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EasyJet_Route_Map-80">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-EasyJet_Website_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EasyJet_Website-81">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Codeshare_agreements">Codeshare agreements</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=EasyJet&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Codeshare agreements">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>In 2013, EasyJet entered a commercial agreement with <a href="/wiki/Transaero_Airlines" class="mw-redirect" title="Transaero Airlines">Transaero Airlines</a> to set up a <a href="/wiki/Codeshare_agreement" title="Codeshare agreement">codeshare agreement</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> whereby Transaero acquired the right to sell a certain number of seats on EasyJet\'s Moscow (Domodedovo) \xe2\x80\x93 London (Gatwick) route. This was the first codeshare agreement for EasyJet; it was terminated when Transaero Airlines ceased to operate in October 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> Citing diminishing demand on the route, EasyJet ceased all flights to Moscow in March 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>EasyJet has a reward miles sharing agreement with <a href="/wiki/Emirates_(airline)" title="Emirates (airline)">Emirates</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Fleet">Fleet</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=EasyJet&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Fleet">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Current_group_fleet">Current group fleet</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span comprises entirely Airbus aircraft. href="#cite_note-87">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-AFI_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AFI-88">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable" style="text-align:center; by July 2019, by EasyJet Europe, which operates 45 Airbus A319 and 91 Airbus A320 aircraft.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup>\nSister company EasyJet Switzerland operates 6 Airbus A319 and 21 Airbus A320 aircraft.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Fleet_strategy_and_aircraft_orders">Fleet strategy and aircraft orders</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=EasyJet&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Fleet strategy and aircraft orders">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In common with other <a href="/wiki/Low-cost_carrier" title="Low-cost carrier">low-cost carriers</a>, EasyJet has a strategy of operating just one aircraft type. Initially it used Boeing 737 aircraft exclusively, but in October 2002 it ordered 120 <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A319" title="Airbus A319">Airbus A319</a> aircraft, plus 120 <a href="/wiki/Option_(aircraft_purchasing)" title="Option (aircraft purchasing)">options</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-KE_19-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KE-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ABORD1_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ABORD1-94">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup> Since then, all orders have been from the Airbus A320 family, and the Boeings have been phased out. With the acquisition of <a href="/wiki/GB_Airways" title="GB Airways">GB Airways</a> in 2007, easyJet inherited nine Airbus A320 and six <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A321" title="Airbus A321">Airbus A321</a> aircraft. This gave the airline some time to evaluate the feasibility of operating these larger aircraft. Based on this evaluation, EasyJet exchanged 25 A319 orders for A320s in July 2008 and later removed the A321 aircraft from the fleet.<sup id="cite_ref-GB1_8-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GB1-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-GB2_28-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GB2-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-GB3_30-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GB3-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-GB4_31-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GB4-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 18 June 2013, the airline announced an intention to acquire &#8211; subject to shareholder approval &#8211; 35 Airbus A320 aircraft, for delivery between 2015 and 2017, and 100 Airbus A320neo aircraft for delivery between 2017 and 2022.<sup id="cite_ref-neo-order_95-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-neo-order-95">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup> As part of the agreement, the airline will have purchase rights on a further 100 A320neo aircraft.<sup id="cite_ref-neo-order_95-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-neo-order-95">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup> The current generation A320s and fifty of the A320neos will replace current A319 aircraft.<sup id="cite_ref-neo-order_95-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-neo-order-95">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 15 May 2017, EasyJet announced the conversion of 30 A320neo orders into A321neo aircraft to be used on busier routes.<sup id="cite_ref-ACF_order_conv_91-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ACF_order_conv-91">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup> The then-CEO of EasyJet, Carolyn McCall, stated of the change: "bigger planes would help EasyJet increase capacity in slot-constrained airports at peak times, such as Geneva, Amsterdam and London Gatwick". She added that the A321neos would help to cut costs by 9 percent.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup> The company took delivery of the first A321neo on 18 July 2018 at the Farnborough International Airshow.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 20 November 2018 EasyJet ordered an additional 17 A320neo, taking their total neo order, including the A321neo, to 147.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 19 November 2019 EasyJet ordered an additional 12 A320neo, taking the total neo orders, including the A321neo, to 159.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:EasyJet_Boeing_737-204;_G-BECG,_January_1997_AXV_(4791175974).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" 1.5x, Airport</a> in January 1997.</div></div></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Historical_fleet">Historical fleet</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a operated the following aircraft:<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable" style="text-align:center; margin-left: auto; Boeing 757-200, briefly leased for the busy summer of 2010.</div></div></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Services">Services</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=EasyJet&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Services">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Booking">Booking</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=EasyJet&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Booking">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Boeing_737-33V,_EasyJet_Airline_AN0219188.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Boeing_737-33V%2C_EasyJet_Airline_AN0219188.jpg/220px-Boeing_737-33V%2C_EasyJet_Airline_AN0219188.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="157" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Boeing_737-33V%2C_EasyJet_Airline_AN0219188.jpg/330px-Boeing_737-33V%2C_EasyJet_Airline_AN0219188.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Boeing_737-33V%2C_EasyJet_Airline_AN0219188.jpg/440px-Boeing_737-33V%2C_EasyJet_Airline_AN0219188.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="731" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Boeing_737-33V,_EasyJet_Airline_AN0219188.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A Boeing 737-33V in telephone number livery.</div></div></div>\n<p>Initially, booking was by telephone only; as a means of promoting this, all of the airline\'s aircraft were painted with the booking telephone number. There is no incentive for <a href="/wiki/Travel_agent" class="mw-redirect" title="Travel agent">travel agents</a> to book flights on the airline because it does not pay <a href="/wiki/Commission_(remuneration)" title="Commission (remuneration)">commissions</a>, which is an industry-standard practice for low-cost carriers.<sup id="cite_ref-KE_19-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KE-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In December 1997, one of EasyJet\'s design and advertising agencies suggested to Stelios Haji-Ioannou that he should consider trialling a website for direct bookings. Haji-Ioannou\'s reply was: "The Internet is for nerds, it will never make money for my business!" Other executives of the airline saw the potential and approved a website trial involving putting a different telephone reservations number on the website to track success. Once Haji-Ioannou saw the results, he changed his mind and an e-commerce website capable of offering real-time online booking went live in April 1998; this was the first such website for a low-cost carrier in Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-KE_19-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KE-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In December 2001, the airline switched from a third-party reservation system to an in-house system.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup> Internet bookings were priced cheaper than booking by telephone to reflect the reduced <a href="/wiki/Call_centre" title="Call centre">call centre</a> costs; as a further means of encouraging use of the website, aircraft were repainted with the web address. Within a year, over 50% of bookings were made using the website; by April 2004, the figure had reportedly jumped to 98%.<sup id="cite_ref-KE_19-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KE-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cabin_and_onboard_services">Cabin and onboard services</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=EasyJet&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Cabin and onboard services">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Easyjet_a319_interior_in_flight_arp.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Easyjet_a319_interior_in_flight_arp.jpg/220px-Easyjet_a319_interior_in_flight_arp.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Easyjet_a319_interior_in_flight_arp.jpg/330px-Easyjet_a319_interior_in_flight_arp.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Easyjet_a319_interior_in_flight_arp.jpg/440px-Easyjet_a319_interior_in_flight_arp.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Easyjet_a319_interior_in_flight_arp.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The cabin of an EasyJet A319, pictured in 2010</div></div></div>\n<p>EasyJet\'s aircraft cabins are configured in a single class, high density layout.<sup id="cite_ref-31952ORD_104-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31952ORD-104">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The airline\'s main fleet, comprising Airbus A319, A320/A320neo and A321neo aircraft, carry up to 156, 180/186 and 235 passengers respectively, depending on layout. A typical Airbus A319 carries approximately 140 passengers in a single class configuration, but as the airline does not serve meals on its shorter flights, it opted for smaller galleys and had a <a href="/wiki/Aircraft_lavatory" title="Aircraft lavatory">lavatory</a> installed in unused space at the rear of the aircraft. The space saved by having smaller galleys allowed for the installation of 156 seats. Due to this seating arrangement, to satisfy safety requirements the airline\'s Airbus A319 aircraft have two pairs of overwing exits, instead of the standard one-pair configuration found on most Airbus A319 aircraft.<sup id="cite_ref-AFI_88-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AFI-88">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-319CAB_105-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-319CAB-105">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-AFD_106-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AFD-106">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>EasyJet does not provide complimentary meals or drinks on its flights (except for some occasional charter flights operated by the airline). Passengers may purchase items on board from the "EasyJet Bistro" <a href="/wiki/Buy_on_board" title="Buy on board">buy on board</a> programme.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup> Onboard sales are an important part of the airline\'s <a href="/wiki/Ancillary_revenue" title="Ancillary revenue">ancillary revenue</a>; gifts such as fragrances, cosmetics, gadgets and EasyJet-branded items are sold on board, as well as tickets for airport transfer services or train tickets. The airline\'s monthly <a href="/wiki/Inflight_magazine" title="Inflight magazine">inflight magazine</a> is called <i>The Traveller</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The airline had previously provided in-flight entertainment (IFE) in some aircraft, such as the ex-GB Airways fleet, using drop-down screens on some Airbus aircraft; by 2018, all use of IFE had been discontinued. The airline offers headphones for purchase, along with a travel pillow and eyeshades, subject to stock. During 2017, \'Air Time\' was introduced on some <a href="/wiki/EasyJet_Switzerland" title="EasyJet Switzerland">EasyJet Switzerland</a> flights, which enables passengers to connect to watch a selection of films and read books through an on-board <a href="/wiki/WiFi" class="mw-redirect" title="WiFi">WiFi</a> network; this service is provided by <a href="/wiki/Rakuten" title="Rakuten">Rakuten</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Frequent_flyer.2C_business_travel_and_loyalty_products"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Frequent_flyer,_business_travel_and_loyalty_products">Frequent flyer, business travel and loyalty products</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=EasyJet&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Frequent flyer, business travel and loyalty products">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Three distinct loyalty products are offered, tailored towards business and frequent flyers. These are Flexi Fare, EasyJet Plus and a new frequent traveller loyalty programme called Flight Club. Flexi Fare<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup> is a type of ticket that is usually more expensive than the regular fare and comparable to a business ticket with other airlines. This ticket offers additional flexibility, including unlimited free date changes within a set period, free route changes, complimentary checked baggage (1x20kg), an increased carry-on baggage allowance, and a \xc2\xa37.50 on board refreshment voucher. EasyJet Plus is an annual subscription product targeted at frequent flyers,<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup> both business and leisure. This service offers free allocated seating (including extra legroom), priority check-in, fast track security, speedy boarding and extra cabin baggage. The airline\'s loyalty programme is called Flight Club.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="EasyJet_Hotels_and_EasyJet_Holidays">EasyJet Hotels and EasyJet Holidays</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=EasyJet&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: EasyJet Hotels and EasyJet Holidays">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>On 14 December 2004, EasyJet and Hotelopia, a subsidiary of <a href="/wiki/First_Choice_(travel_firm)" class="mw-redirect" title="First Choice (travel firm)">First Choice Holidays</a>, launched the co-branded EasyJetHotels accommodation booking service. EasyJetHotels offers accommodation products throughout the airline\'s network. Customers booking flights through the airline\'s website are provided with quotes for a number of hotels at their destination. Alternatively, customers can book accommodation separately at the EasyJetHotels website.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 28 June 2007, the airline expanded its relationship with Hotelopia by launching EasyJetHolidays, which offers Travel Trust Association protected <a href="/wiki/Package_holiday" class="mw-redirect" title="Package holiday">package holidays</a> made up of EasyJet flights and Hotelopia accommodation products.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 6 November 2010, the airline started a venture with Low Cost Travel Group, to offer flights dynamically packaged with Low Cost Travel Group\'s accommodation through the EasyJet Holidays website. As of March 2011, EasyJet Holidays has provided holidays and city breaks to all of the airline\'s routes.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>\nA mid November 2019 report indicated that the company planned to relaunch the package holiday business, after the bankruptcy of former competitor <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Cook_Group" title="Thomas Cook Group">Thomas Cook</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup></p><blockquote><p>"The total European package holidays market is worth around \xc2\xa361bn per year ... we know customers want holidays with various durations and not the traditional seven and 14 nights. The UK alone is a \xc2\xa313bn market and has grown by 6% annually," according to a company spokesperson.</p></blockquote>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=EasyJet&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: References">edit</a><span
